  "content": "# Technical Design Proposal: Migration from In-Memory Event Bus to External Message Broker\n\n**Document ID:** PROPOSAL-2026-001\n**Project:** UtilityChain Core Suite\n**Author:** Senior Solutions Architect\n**Date:** February 2, 2026\n**Status:** Draft for Review\n\n---\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nThis proposal outlines a comprehensive migration strategy for the UtilityChain Core Suite's inter-service communication infrastructure. The current `InMemoryEventBus` implementation, while performant for single-node deployments, presents significant scalability and resilience limitations as the platform approaches mainnet launch. This document details the technical approach, affected components, consistency patterns, configuration changes, error handling strategies, and architectural trade-offs for migrating to an external message broker.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Analysis of Current Architecture\n\n### 1.1 Current Implementation Overview\n\nAs documented in **ADR-003 (Event-Driven Module Communication)** at `docs/adr/003-event-driven-module-communication.md`, the UtilityChain Core Suite employs a lightweight, in-memory Domain Event Bus following the Mediator and Observer patterns. The system was intentionally designed for in-process communication to achieve:\n\n- **Zero-copy data-flow** for maximum throughput\n- **Sub-millisecond latency** for consensus-critical operations\n- **Single-binary deployment** without external dependencies\n\n### 1.2 IEventBus Interface Contracts\n\nThe codebase contains multiple `IEventBus` interface definitions, reflecting the modular monolith architecture:\n\n**Core Abstractions** (`src/UtilityChain.Core/Abstractions/IEventBus.cs:43-88`):\n```csharp\npublic interface IEventBus\n{\n    ValueTask PublishAsync<TEvent>(TEvent @event, CancellationToken ct = default)\n        where TEvent : class, IEvent;\n\n    SubscriptionToken Subscribe<TEvent>(\n        Func<TEvent, CancellationToken, ValueTask> handler,\n        SubscriptionOptions? options = null)\n        where TEvent : class, IEvent;\n\n    void Unsubscribe(in SubscriptionToken token);\n}\n```\n\n**Core Services Implementation** (`src/UtilityChain.Core/Services/InMemoryEventBus.cs:36-75`):\n```csharp\npublic interface IEventBus : IAsyncDisposable, IDisposable\n{\n    IDisposable Subscribe<TEvent>(\n        Func<TEvent, CancellationToken, ValueTask> handler,\n        string? subscriberId = null)\n        where TEvent : IEvent;\n\n    ValueTask PublishAsync<TEvent>(TEvent @event, CancellationToken cancellationToken = default)\n        where TEvent : IEvent;\n\n    bool HasSubscribers(Type eventType);\n}\n```\n\n### 1.3 InMemoryEventBus Implementation Characteristics\n\nThe primary implementation at `src/UtilityChain.Core/Services/InMemoryEventBus.cs:82-351` exhibits these characteristics:\n\n1. **Channel-Based Architecture**: Uses `System.Threading.Channels.Channel<EventEnvelope>` with bounded capacity (default 65,536)\n2. **Multi-Dispatcher Model**: Spawns `Environment.ProcessorCount` dispatcher tasks for parallel processing\n3. **Fire-and-Forget Delivery**: Each handler executes via `Task.Run()` independently (lines 262-281)\n4. **Weak Reference Subscriptions**: Prevents memory leaks but complicates handler lifecycle management\n5. **In-Process Only**: All communication occurs within the same address space\n\n**Critical Limitation:** The synchronous coupling between state mutations and event publication creates an atomic boundary that will be broken when introducing an external broker.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Affected Components (IEventBus Usage Analysis)\n\n### 2.1 Services That Publish Events\n\n| Service | File Location | Events Published | Nature of Changes Required |\n|---------|--------------|------------------|---------------------------|\n| **StakingService** | `src/UtilityChain.Staking/StakingService.cs:31,50,93,136,208` | `StakeCreatedEvent`, `StakeWithdrawnEvent`, `RewardsClaimedEvent` | Implement outbox pattern for stake operations |\n| **GovernanceService** | `src/UtilityChain.Governance/GovernanceService.cs:36,44,80,130,199` | `ProposalCreatedEvent`, `VoteCastEvent`, `ProposalFinalizedEvent` | Wrap proposal/vote transactions with outbox writes |\n| **TransactionProcessor** | `src/UtilityChain.TransactionProcessing/TransactionProcessor.cs:29,43,125,134,163` | `TransactionRejectedEvent`, `TransactionAcceptedEvent` | Critical path - requires careful outbox integration |\n| **P2PService** | `src/UtilityChain.Networking/P2PService.cs:34,44,240,268,348` | `PeerConnectedEvent`, `PeerDisconnectedEvent`, `NetworkMessageEvent` | Network events can tolerate eventual consistency |\n| **TokenService** | `src/UtilityChain.Tokens/TokenService.cs:27,39,63,98` | `TokenCreatedEvent`, `TokenMintedEvent`, `TokenBurnedEvent`, `TokenTransferredEvent` | Must coordinate with token state persistence |\n| **ConsensusContext** | `src/UtilityChain.Consensus/ConsensusContext.cs:41,58,235` | `BlockProposedEvent` | Consensus-critical; may require hybrid approach |\n| **WorldState** | `src/UtilityChain.Core/State/WorldState.cs:140,152,284` | `WorldStateCommittedEvent` | State root publication must be atomic with commit |\n| **GatewayController** | `src/UtilityChain.ApiGateway/GatewayController.cs:21,28,91,161,196` | `TransactionReceived`, `ContractDeployed`, `ContractInvoked` | API events can be published asynchronously |\n\n### 2.2 Services That Subscribe to Events\n\n| Service | Events Subscribed | Critical Path? |\n|---------|------------------|----------------|\n| **StakingService** | `NewBlockEvent` (line 65) | Yes - reward calculations |\n| **GovernanceService** | `ProposalCreatedEvent`, `ProposalFinalizedEvent` (lines 52-53) | Yes - policy enforcement |\n| **ConsensusContext** | `BlockCommittedEvent`, `VoteReceivedEvent` (lines 80-81) | Critical - consensus integrity |\n| **TokenService** | `BlockMinedEvent` (line 98) | Yes - balance commits |\n| **NodeRuntimeCoordinator** | `NodePanicEvent` (`Startup.cs:241`) | Critical - node lifecycle |\n\n### 2.3 Summary of Changes by Severity\n\n**High Impact (Requires Transactional Outbox):**\n- `TransactionProcessor` - Transaction acceptance must be atomic with event publication\n- `StakingService` - Stake operations affect account balances\n- `GovernanceService` - Votes must be recorded durably before notification\n- `WorldState` - State root changes are authoritative\n\n**Medium Impact (Requires Reliable Publishing):**\n- `TokenService` - Token operations should be durable\n- `ConsensusContext` - Block proposals need reliable delivery\n\n**Low Impact (Fire-and-Forget Acceptable):**\n- `P2PService` - Network events are observational\n- `GatewayController` - API notifications are advisory\n\n---\n\n## 3. Asynchronicity and Data Consistency: The Transactional Outbox Pattern\n\n### 3.1 The Atomicity Problem\n\nThe current `InMemoryEventBus` provides implicit atomicity: if `PublishAsync` succeeds, the event is delivered (assuming the process doesn't crash). Consider this flow in `TransactionProcessor.cs:141-163`:\n\n```csharp\n// Current Flow (PROBLEMATIC with external broker):\nawait _repository.AddPendingAsync(tx, ct);  // Step 1: Persist\nawait _eventBus.PublishAsync(new TransactionAcceptedEvent(tx), ct);  // Step 2: Publish\n```\n\nWith an external broker, this creates a dual-write problem:\n- If Step 1 succeeds but Step 2 fails (network partition), the transaction is persisted but never announced\n- If Step 2 succeeds but Step 1 fails (DB error), an event is published for a non-existent transaction\n\n### 3.2 Proposed Solution: Transactional Outbox Pattern\n\nThe **Transactional Outbox Pattern** ensures atomicity by writing events to a local \"outbox\" table within the same database transaction as the business operation. A separate background process (\"Outbox Publisher\") then reliably forwards these events to the external broker.\n\n#### 3.2.1 Outbox Entity Design\n\n```csharp\n// src/UtilityChain.Core/Outbox/OutboxMessage.cs\nnamespace UtilityChain.Core.Outbox;\n\npublic sealed class OutboxMessage\n{\n    public Guid Id { get; init; } = Guid.NewGuid();\n    public string EventType { get; init; } = default!;\n    public string Payload { get; init; } = default!;  // JSON-serialized event\n    public DateTimeOffset CreatedAt { get; init; } = DateTimeOffset.UtcNow;\n    public DateTimeOffset? ProcessedAt { get; set; }\n    public int RetryCount { get; set; }\n    public string? LastError { get; set; }\n    public OutboxMessageStatus Status { get; set; } = OutboxMessageStatus.Pending;\n}\n\npublic enum OutboxMessageStatus\n{\n    Pending,\n    Processing,\n    Completed,\n    Failed\n}\n```\n\n#### 3.2.2 Outbox Repository Interface\n\n```csharp\n// src/UtilityChain.Core/Outbox/IOutboxRepository.cs\nnamespace UtilityChain.Core.Outbox;\n\npublic interface IOutboxRepository\n{\n    Task AddAsync(OutboxMessage message, CancellationToken ct = default);\n    Task<IReadOnlyList<OutboxMessage>> GetPendingAsync(int batchSize, CancellationToken ct = default);\n    Task MarkAsProcessedAsync(Guid id, CancellationToken ct = default);\n    Task MarkAsFailedAsync(Guid id, string error, CancellationToken ct = default);\n}\n```\n\n#### 3.2.3 Modified Transaction Processing Flow\n\n```csharp\n// src/UtilityChain.TransactionProcessing/TransactionProcessor.cs (Modified)\nprivate async Task HandleTransactionAsync(TransactionEnvelope envelope, CancellationToken ct)\n{\n    var tx = envelope.Transaction;\n\n    // ... validation logic ...\n\n    // CRITICAL CHANGE: Use database transaction for atomicity\n    await using var dbTransaction = await _repository.BeginTransactionAsync(ct);\n    try\n    {\n        // Step 1: Persist transaction\n        await _repository.AddPendingAsync(tx, ct);\n\n        // Step 2: Write to outbox (SAME transaction)\n        var outboxMessage = new OutboxMessage\n        {\n            EventType = typeof(TransactionAcceptedEvent).FullName!,\n            Payload = JsonSerializer.Serialize(new TransactionAcceptedEvent(tx))\n        };\n        await _outboxRepository.AddAsync(outboxMessage, ct);\n\n        // Step 3: Commit both together\n        await dbTransaction.CommitAsync(ct);\n    }\n    catch\n    {\n        await dbTransaction.RollbackAsync(ct);\n        throw;\n    }\n\n    // Event will be published by OutboxPublisher background service\n}\n```\n\n#### 3.2.4 Outbox Publisher Background Service\n\n```csharp\n// src/UtilityChain.Infrastructure/Messaging/OutboxPublisher.cs\nnamespace UtilityChain.Infrastructure.Messaging;\n\npublic sealed class OutboxPublisher : BackgroundService\n{\n    private readonly IOutboxRepository _outboxRepository;\n    private readonly IMessageBrokerClient _brokerClient;\n    private readonly ILogger<OutboxPublisher> _logger;\n    private readonly OutboxPublisherOptions _options;\n\n    protected override async Task ExecuteAsync(CancellationToken stoppingToken)\n    {\n        while (!stoppingToken.IsCancellationRequested)\n        {\n            try\n            {\n                var messages = await _outboxRepository\n                    .GetPendingAsync(_options.BatchSize, stoppingToken);\n\n                foreach (var message in messages)\n                {\n                    try\n                    {\n                        await _brokerClient.PublishAsync(\n                            message.EventType,\n                            message.Payload,\n                            stoppingToken);\n\n                        await _outboxRepository.MarkAsProcessedAsync(message.Id, stoppingToken);\n                    }\n                    catch (Exception ex)\n                    {\n                        _logger.LogError(ex,\n                            \"Failed to publish outbox message {MessageId}\", message.Id);\n                        await _outboxRepository.MarkAsFailedAsync(\n                            message.Id, ex.Message, stoppingToken);\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n            catch (Exception ex)\n            {\n                _logger.LogError(ex, \"Outbox publisher iteration failed\");\n            }\n\n            await Task.Delay(_options.PollingInterval, stoppingToken);\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### 3.3 Consistency Guarantees\n\n| Scenario | Behavior with Outbox Pattern |\n|----------|------------------------------|\n| DB commit succeeds, broker unavailable | Event stored in outbox, delivered when broker recovers |\n| DB commit fails | No outbox entry, no event published (consistent) |\n| Outbox publisher crashes mid-batch | Uncommitted messages remain pending, re-processed on restart |\n| Duplicate delivery to broker | Consumers must be idempotent (handled via event ID) |\n\n---\n\n## 4. Configuration and Dependency Management\n\n### 4.1 appsettings.json Modifications\n\nCurrent configuration at `src/UtilityChain.Node/appsettings.json:97-103`:\n```json\n\"EventBus\": {\n  \"Implementation\": \"UtilityChain.Infrastructure.Eventing.InMemoryEventBus\",\n  \"BufferSize\": 8192,\n  \"RetryPolicy\": {\n    \"RetryCount\": 5,\n    \"BaseDelayMilliseconds\": 200\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**Proposed Configuration:**\n```json\n{\n  \"UtilityChain\": {\n    \"Node\": {\n      \"EventBus\": {\n        \"Implementation\": \"UtilityChain.Infrastructure.Eventing.RabbitMQEventBus\",\n        \"BufferSize\": 8192,\n        \"RetryPolicy\": {\n          \"RetryCount\": 5,\n          \"BaseDelayMilliseconds\": 200,\n          \"MaxDelayMilliseconds\": 30000,\n          \"ExponentialBackoff\": true\n        }\n      },\n      \"MessageBroker\": {\n        \"Provider\": \"RabbitMQ\",\n        \"RabbitMQ\": {\n          \"HostName\": \"rabbitmq.consortium.local\",\n          \"Port\": 5672,\n          \"VirtualHost\": \"/utilitychain\",\n          \"UserName\": \"uc_publisher\",\n          \"Password\": \"${RABBITMQ_PASSWORD}\",\n          \"UseTls\": true,\n          \"TlsCertPath\": \"/etc/ssl/certs/rabbitmq-client.pfx\",\n          \"ConnectionRetryCount\": 10,\n          \"ConnectionRetryIntervalSeconds\": 5,\n          \"HeartbeatSeconds\": 60,\n          \"PrefetchCount\": 100,\n          \"PublisherConfirms\": true\n        },\n        \"Exchanges\": {\n          \"DomainEvents\": {\n            \"Name\": \"utilitychain.domain.events\",\n            \"Type\": \"topic\",\n            \"Durable\": true\n          },\n          \"DeadLetter\": {\n            \"Name\": \"utilitychain.dlx\",\n            \"Type\": \"fanout\",\n            \"Durable\": true\n          }\n        },\n        \"Queues\": {\n          \"StakingEvents\": {\n            \"Name\": \"utilitychain.staking.events\",\n            \"Durable\": true,\n            \"RoutingKeys\": [\"staking.*\"],\n            \"DeadLetterExchange\": \"utilitychain.dlx\",\n            \"MessageTtlSeconds\": 86400\n          },\n          \"GovernanceEvents\": {\n            \"Name\": \"utilitychain.governance.events\",\n            \"Durable\": true,\n            \"RoutingKeys\": [\"governance.*\"],\n            \"DeadLetterExchange\": \"utilitychain.dlx\"\n          },\n          \"TransactionEvents\": {\n            \"Name\": \"utilitychain.transactions.events\",\n            \"Durable\": true,\n            \"RoutingKeys\": [\"transaction.*\"],\n            \"DeadLetterExchange\": \"utilitychain.dlx\"\n          },\n          \"ConsensusEvents\": {\n            \"Name\": \"utilitychain.consensus.events\",\n            \"Durable\": true,\n            \"RoutingKeys\": [\"consensus.*\", \"block.*\"],\n            \"DeadLetterExchange\": \"utilitychain.dlx\"\n          }\n        }\n      },\n      \"Outbox\": {\n        \"Enabled\": true,\n        \"PollingIntervalMilliseconds\": 500,\n        \"BatchSize\": 100,\n        \"MaxRetryCount\": 5,\n        \"CleanupIntervalHours\": 24,\n        \"RetentionDays\": 7\n      }\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### 4.2 Startup.cs / Program.cs Modifications\n\n**Current Registration** (`src/UtilityChain.Node/Startup.cs:101`):\n```csharp\nservices.AddSingleton<IEventBus, InMemoryEventBus>();\n```\n\n**Proposed Registration:**\n```csharp\n// src/UtilityChain.Node/Startup.cs (Modified)\nusing Microsoft.Extensions.DependencyInjection;\nusing UtilityChain.Infrastructure.Messaging;\nusing UtilityChain.Infrastructure.Messaging.RabbitMQ;\nusing UtilityChain.Core.Outbox;\n\npublic static class EventBusServiceExtensions\n{\n    public static IServiceCollection AddEventBusInfrastructure(\n        this IServiceCollection services,\n        IConfiguration configuration)\n    {\n        // Bind options\n        services.Configure<MessageBrokerOptions>(\n            configuration.GetSection(\"UtilityChain:Node:MessageBroker\"));\n        services.Configure<OutboxOptions>(\n            configuration.GetSection(\"UtilityChain:Node:Outbox\"));\n\n        // Register outbox infrastructure\n        services.AddScoped<IOutboxRepository, SqliteOutboxRepository>();\n        services.AddHostedService<OutboxPublisher>();\n        services.AddHostedService<OutboxCleanupService>();\n\n        // Register message broker client\n        var brokerProvider = configuration\n            .GetValue<string>(\"UtilityChain:Node:MessageBroker:Provider\");\n\n        switch (brokerProvider?.ToLowerInvariant())\n        {\n            case \"rabbitmq\":\n                services.AddSingleton<IMessageBrokerClient, RabbitMQClient>();\n                services.AddSingleton<IEventBus, RabbitMQEventBus>();\n                services.AddHealthChecks()\n                    .AddRabbitMQ(name: \"rabbitmq\", tags: new[] { \"messaging\" });\n                break;\n\n            case \"kafka\":\n                services.AddSingleton<IMessageBrokerClient, KafkaClient>();\n                services.AddSingleton<IEventBus, KafkaEventBus>();\n                services.AddHealthChecks()\n                    .AddKafka(name: \"kafka\", tags: new[] { \"messaging\" });\n                break;\n\n            case \"inmemory\":\n            default:\n                // Fallback for development/testing\n                services.AddSingleton<IEventBus, InMemoryEventBus>();\n                break;\n        }\n\n        // Register dead-letter queue handler\n        services.AddHostedService<DeadLetterQueueProcessor>();\n\n        return services;\n    }\n}\n\n// In BuildHost method:\n.ConfigureServices((ctx, services) =>\n{\n    // ... existing registrations ...\n\n    // Replace: services.AddSingleton<IEventBus, InMemoryEventBus>();\n    // With:\n    services.AddEventBusInfrastructure(ctx.Configuration);\n\n    // ... rest of registrations ...\n})\n```\n\n### 4.3 RabbitMQ Client Implementation Skeleton\n\n```csharp\n// src/UtilityChain.Infrastructure/Messaging/RabbitMQ/RabbitMQEventBus.cs\nnamespace UtilityChain.Infrastructure.Messaging.RabbitMQ;\n\npublic sealed class RabbitMQEventBus : IEventBus, IAsyncDisposable\n{\n    private readonly IConnection _connection;\n    private readonly IModel _publishChannel;\n    private readonly ConcurrentDictionary<Type, IModel> _consumeChannels;\n    private readonly MessageBrokerOptions _options;\n    private readonly ILogger<RabbitMQEventBus> _logger;\n    private readonly JsonSerializerOptions _jsonOptions;\n\n    public RabbitMQEventBus(\n        IOptions<MessageBrokerOptions> options,\n        ILogger<RabbitMQEventBus> logger)\n    {\n        _options = options.Value;\n        _logger = logger;\n        _jsonOptions = new JsonSerializerOptions\n        {\n            PropertyNamingPolicy = JsonNamingPolicy.CamelCase\n        };\n        _consumeChannels = new();\n\n        var factory = new ConnectionFactory\n        {\n            HostName = _options.RabbitMQ.HostName,\n            Port = _options.RabbitMQ.Port,\n            VirtualHost = _options.RabbitMQ.VirtualHost,\n            UserName = _options.RabbitMQ.UserName,\n            Password = _options.RabbitMQ.Password,\n            AutomaticRecoveryEnabled = true,\n            NetworkRecoveryInterval = TimeSpan.FromSeconds(10)\n        };\n\n        _connection = factory.CreateConnection();\n        _publishChannel = _connection.CreateModel();\n\n        // Enable publisher confirms for reliable delivery\n        _publishChannel.ConfirmSelect();\n\n        DeclareTopology();\n    }\n\n    public async ValueTask PublishAsync<TEvent>(\n        TEvent @event,\n        CancellationToken cancellationToken = default)\n        where TEvent : IEvent\n    {\n        var routingKey = GetRoutingKey(typeof(TEvent));\n        var body = JsonSerializer.SerializeToUtf8Bytes(@event, _jsonOptions);\n\n        var properties = _publishChannel.CreateBasicProperties();\n        properties.DeliveryMode = 2; // Persistent\n        properties.MessageId = Guid.NewGuid().ToString();\n        properties.Timestamp = new AmqpTimestamp(DateTimeOffset.UtcNow.ToUnixTimeSeconds());\n        properties.Type = typeof(TEvent).FullName;\n\n        _publishChannel.BasicPublish(\n            exchange: _options.Exchanges.DomainEvents.Name,\n            routingKey: routingKey,\n            basicProperties: properties,\n            body: body);\n\n        // Wait for broker acknowledgment\n        _publishChannel.WaitForConfirmsOrDie(TimeSpan.FromSeconds(5));\n\n        await Task.CompletedTask;\n    }\n\n    public IDisposable Subscribe<TEvent>(\n        Func<TEvent, CancellationToken, ValueTask> handler,\n        string? subscriberId = null)\n        where TEvent : IEvent\n    {\n        var eventType = typeof(TEvent);\n        var queueName = GetQueueName(eventType);\n\n        var channel = _connection.CreateModel();\n        _consumeChannels[eventType] = channel;\n\n        var consumer = new AsyncEventingBasicConsumer(channel);\n        consumer.Received += async (model, ea) =>\n        {\n            try\n            {\n                var @event = JsonSerializer.Deserialize<TEvent>(ea.Body.Span, _jsonOptions);\n                if (@event != null)\n                {\n                    await handler(@event, CancellationToken.None);\n                }\n                channel.BasicAck(ea.DeliveryTag, false);\n            }\n            catch (Exception ex)\n            {\n                _logger.LogError(ex, \"Error processing message {MessageId}\", ea.BasicProperties.MessageId);\n                // Negative acknowledgment - message will go to DLQ\n                channel.BasicNack(ea.DeliveryTag, false, false);\n            }\n        };\n\n        channel.BasicConsume(queue: queueName, autoAck: false, consumer: consumer);\n\n        return new SubscriptionHandle(() =>\n        {\n            if (_consumeChannels.TryRemove(eventType, out var ch))\n            {\n                ch.Close();\n                ch.Dispose();\n            }\n        });\n    }\n\n    private void DeclareTopology()\n    {\n        // Declare main exchange\n        _publishChannel.ExchangeDeclare(\n            exchange: _options.Exchanges.DomainEvents.Name,\n            type: _options.Exchanges.DomainEvents.Type,\n            durable: true);\n\n        // Declare dead-letter exchange\n        _publishChannel.ExchangeDeclare(\n            exchange: _options.Exchanges.DeadLetter.Name,\n            type: \"fanout\",\n            durable: true);\n\n        // Declare dead-letter queue\n        _publishChannel.QueueDeclare(\n            queue: \"utilitychain.dlq\",\n            durable: true,\n            exclusive: false,\n            autoDelete: false);\n        _publishChannel.QueueBind(\"utilitychain.dlq\", _options.Exchanges.DeadLetter.Name, \"\");\n\n        // Declare application queues with DLX binding\n        foreach (var queueConfig in _options.Queues.Values)\n        {\n            var args = new Dictionary<string, object>\n            {\n                [\"x-dead-letter-exchange\"] = _options.Exchanges.DeadLetter.Name\n            };\n\n            if (queueConfig.MessageTtlSeconds > 0)\n            {\n                args[\"x-message-ttl\"] = queueConfig.MessageTtlSeconds * 1000;\n            }\n\n            _publishChannel.QueueDeclare(\n                queue: queueConfig.Name,\n                durable: queueConfig.Durable,\n                exclusive: false,\n                autoDelete: false,\n                arguments: args);\n\n            foreach (var routingKey in queueConfig.RoutingKeys)\n            {\n                _publishChannel.QueueBind(\n                    queueConfig.Name,\n                    _options.Exchanges.DomainEvents.Name,\n                    routingKey);\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    private static string GetRoutingKey(Type eventType)\n    {\n        // Example: TransactionAcceptedEvent -> transaction.accepted\n        var name = eventType.Name.Replace(\"Event\", \"\");\n        return string.Join(\".\",\n            System.Text.RegularExpressions.Regex\n                .Split(name, \"(?<!^)(?=[A-Z])\")\n                .Select(s => s.ToLowerInvariant()));\n    }\n\n    public async ValueTask DisposeAsync()\n    {\n        foreach (var channel in _consumeChannels.Values)\n        {\n            channel.Close();\n            channel.Dispose();\n        }\n        _publishChannel.Close();\n        _publishChannel.Dispose();\n        _connection.Close();\n        _connection.Dispose();\n        await Task.CompletedTask;\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. Resilience and Error Handling\n\n### 5.1 New Failure Modes with External Broker\n\n| Failure Mode | Description | Impact | Mitigation |\n|--------------|-------------|--------|------------|\n| **Network Partition** | Node loses connectivity to broker | Events queued in outbox, not delivered | Outbox pattern with local persistence |\n| **Broker Downtime** | RabbitMQ/Kafka cluster unavailable | All event publishing blocked | Connection retry with exponential backoff |\n| **Message Expiration** | TTL exceeded before consumption | Events lost | Dead-letter queue for inspection |\n| **Poison Messages** | Malformed events causing consumer failures | Consumer stuck in retry loop | Dead-letter after N retries |\n| **Consumer Lag** | Consumers slower than publishers | Queue growth, memory pressure | Prefetch limits, consumer scaling |\n| **Duplicate Delivery** | Broker redelivers after timeout | Handler invoked multiple times | Idempotent handlers (deduplication) |\n\n### 5.2 Dead-Letter Queue (DLQ) Strategy\n\nMessages that cannot be processed after exhausting retry attempts are routed to a Dead-Letter Queue for manual inspection and replay.\n\n```csharp\n// src/UtilityChain.Infrastructure/Messaging/DeadLetterQueueProcessor.cs\nnamespace UtilityChain.Infrastructure.Messaging;\n\npublic sealed class DeadLetterQueueProcessor : BackgroundService\n{\n    private readonly IMessageBrokerClient _brokerClient;\n    private readonly IDeadLetterRepository _dlqRepository;\n    private readonly ILogger<DeadLetterQueueProcessor> _logger;\n\n    protected override async Task ExecuteAsync(CancellationToken stoppingToken)\n    {\n        await _brokerClient.ConsumeAsync<DeadLetterMessage>(\n            \"utilitychain.dlq\",\n            async (message, ct) =>\n            {\n                _logger.LogWarning(\n                    \"Dead letter received: Type={EventType}, OriginalError={Error}\",\n                    message.OriginalType,\n                    message.LastError);\n\n                // Persist for manual review/replay\n                await _dlqRepository.StoreAsync(new DeadLetterRecord\n                {\n                    Id = Guid.NewGuid(),\n                    OriginalEventType = message.OriginalType,\n                    Payload = message.Payload,\n                    FailedAt = DateTimeOffset.UtcNow,\n                    RetryCount = message.RetryCount,\n                    LastError = message.LastError,\n                    OriginalQueue = message.OriginalQueue\n                }, ct);\n            },\n            stoppingToken);\n    }\n}\n\npublic interface IDeadLetterRepository\n{\n    Task StoreAsync(DeadLetterRecord record, CancellationToken ct);\n    Task<IReadOnlyList<DeadLetterRecord>> GetPendingReplayAsync(int limit, CancellationToken ct);\n    Task ReplayAsync(Guid id, CancellationToken ct);\n    Task DiscardAsync(Guid id, string reason, CancellationToken ct);\n}\n```\n\n### 5.3 Retry Policies with Polly\n\n```csharp\n// src/UtilityChain.Infrastructure/Messaging/ResiliencePolicies.cs\nusing Polly;\nusing Polly.Retry;\n\nnamespace UtilityChain.Infrastructure.Messaging;\n\npublic static class ResiliencePolicies\n{\n    public static AsyncRetryPolicy CreatePublishPolicy(ILogger logger, RetryPolicyOptions options)\n    {\n        return Policy\n            .Handle<BrokerUnreachableException>()\n            .Or<AlreadyClosedException>()\n            .Or<IOException>()\n            .WaitAndRetryAsync(\n                retryCount: options.RetryCount,\n                sleepDurationProvider: attempt =>\n                {\n                    var delay = TimeSpan.FromMilliseconds(\n                        Math.Min(\n                            options.BaseDelayMilliseconds * Math.Pow(2, attempt),\n                            options.MaxDelayMilliseconds));\n\n                    // Add jitter to prevent thundering herd\n                    var jitter = TimeSpan.FromMilliseconds(\n                        Random.Shared.Next(0, (int)(delay.TotalMilliseconds * 0.1)));\n\n                    return delay + jitter;\n                },\n                onRetry: (exception, delay, attempt, context) =>\n                {\n                    logger.LogWarning(exception,\n                        \"Event publish attempt {Attempt} failed. Retrying in {Delay}ms\",\n                        attempt, delay.TotalMilliseconds);\n                });\n    }\n\n    public static AsyncRetryPolicy CreateConsumePolicy(ILogger logger, int maxRetries)\n    {\n        return Policy\n            .Handle<Exception>(ex => !(ex is OperationCanceledException))\n            .WaitAndRetryAsync(\n                retryCount: maxRetries,\n                sleepDurationProvider: attempt =>\n                    TimeSpan.FromSeconds(Math.Pow(2, attempt)),\n                onRetry: (exception, delay, attempt, context) =>\n                {\n                    logger.LogWarning(exception,\n                        \"Event consumption attempt {Attempt} failed. Retrying in {Delay}s\",\n                        attempt, delay.TotalSeconds);\n                });\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### 5.4 Idempotent Event Handlers\n\nTo handle duplicate deliveries, consumers must be idempotent:\n\n```csharp\n// Example: Idempotent StakingService event handler\npublic class IdempotentStakingEventHandler : IEventHandler<StakeCreatedEvent>\n{\n    private readonly IProcessedEventRepository _processedEvents;\n    private readonly IStakeAggregator _aggregator;\n\n    public async ValueTask HandleAsync(StakeCreatedEvent @event, CancellationToken ct)\n    {\n        // Check if already processed\n        var eventId = @event.EventId; // Events should carry a unique ID\n        if (await _processedEvents.ExistsAsync(eventId, ct))\n        {\n            return; // Idempotent: skip duplicate\n        }\n\n        // Process the event\n        await _aggregator.ApplyStakeAsync(@event.Stake, ct);\n\n        // Mark as processed\n        await _processedEvents.MarkAsync(eventId, ct);\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 6. Architectural Trade-offs\n\n### 6.1 Advantages of External Message Broker\n\n| Benefit | Description |\n|---------|-------------|\n| **Horizontal Scalability** | Multiple node instances can publish/consume independently, enabling cluster deployments |\n| **Temporal Decoupling** | Publishers and consumers operate independently; consumers can catch up after downtime |\n| **Durable Message Storage** | Messages persist in broker until acknowledged, surviving node restarts |\n| **Independent Deployments** | Services can be updated without coordinating all components simultaneously |\n| **Observability** | Broker management consoles provide queue depths, throughput metrics, consumer lag visibility |\n| **Replay Capability** | Ability to replay events from DLQ or persistent topics (Kafka) for debugging or reprocessing |\n| **Multi-Protocol Support** | External clients (monitoring, analytics) can subscribe without coupling to .NET internals |\n\n### 6.2 Disadvantages and New Complexities\n\n| Drawback | Description | Mitigation |\n|----------|-------------|------------|\n| **Increased Latency** | Network round-trips add 1-10ms overhead vs. in-memory microseconds | Accept for non-critical paths; hybrid approach for consensus |\n| **Operational Complexity** | New infrastructure to deploy, monitor, and maintain | Infrastructure-as-Code, managed services (CloudAMQP, Confluent Cloud) |\n| **Data Consistency Complexity** | Dual-write problem requires outbox pattern | Implement as described in Section 3 |\n| **Eventual Consistency** | Consumers may see events with delay | Design handlers for idempotency; use compensation patterns |\n| **New Failure Modes** | Broker failures, network partitions, poison messages | DLQ, retries, circuit breakers (Section 5) |\n| **Cost** | Additional infrastructure cost (VMs, managed services) | Size appropriately; start with single-node broker for consortium |\n| **Message Ordering** | Global ordering not guaranteed across partitions/queues | Use partition keys for ordered streams where required |\n| **Serialization Overhead** | Events must be serialized to JSON/Protobuf | Use efficient serializers; schema registry for versioning |\n\n### 6.3 Hybrid Approach Recommendation\n\nFor **consensus-critical events** (block proposals, vote collection), consider maintaining a supplementary in-process channel:\n\n```csharp\npublic sealed class HybridEventBus : IEventBus\n{\n    private readonly InMemoryEventBus _inProcess;\n    private readonly RabbitMQEventBus _distributed;\n    private readonly HashSet<Type> _localOnlyTypes = new()\n    {\n        typeof(VoteReceivedEvent),\n        typeof(BlockProposedEvent)\n    };\n\n    public async ValueTask PublishAsync<TEvent>(TEvent @event, CancellationToken ct)\n        where TEvent : IEvent\n    {\n        // Consensus-critical events: local only for latency\n        if (_localOnlyTypes.Contains(typeof(TEvent)))\n        {\n            await _inProcess.PublishAsync(@event, ct);\n            return;\n        }\n\n        // All other events: distributed for durability\n        await _distributed.PublishAsync(@event, ct);\n\n        // Optionally also publish locally for immediate in-node handling\n        await _inProcess.PublishAsync(@event, ct);\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 7. Migration Plan Summary\n\n### Phase 1: Foundation (Week 1-2)\n1. Implement `IOutboxRepository` with SQLite/PostgreSQL backing\n2. Create `OutboxMessage` entity and database migrations\n3. Build `OutboxPublisher` background service\n4. Add comprehensive unit tests for outbox patterns\n\n### Phase 2: Broker Integration (Week 3-4)\n1. Implement `IMessageBrokerClient` interface\n2. Build `RabbitMQEventBus` implementation\n3. Configure queue topology (exchanges, queues, DLX)\n4. Set up local RabbitMQ for development\n\n### Phase 3: Service Migration (Week 5-7)\n1. Migrate low-risk services first (P2PService, GatewayController)\n2. Add outbox writes to medium-risk services (TokenService, GovernanceService)\n3. Migrate high-risk services (TransactionProcessor, StakingService)\n4. Implement hybrid approach for ConsensusContext\n\n### Phase 4: Testing & Hardening (Week 8)\n1. Chaos testing (broker failures, network partitions)\n2. Load testing with production-like traffic\n3. DLQ monitoring and alerting\n4. Runbook documentation for operations\n\n### Phase 5: Production Rollout (Week 9-10)\n1. Deploy broker infrastructure\n2. Feature flag rollout (gradual traffic shift)\n3. Monitor queue depths and consumer lag\n4. Full cutover and InMemoryEventBus deprecation\n\n---\n\n## 8. Conclusion\n\nThe migration from `InMemoryEventBus` to an external message broker represents a significant architectural evolution for the UtilityChain Core Suite. While introducing operational complexity and new failure modes, the benefits of scalability, resilience, and independent deployability are essential for mainnet readiness.\n\nThe **Transactional Outbox Pattern** is the cornerstone of this migration, ensuring data consistency despite the inherently asynchronous nature of distributed messaging. Combined with robust retry policies, dead-letter queues, and idempotent consumers, the proposed architecture provides enterprise-grade reliability.\n\nFor consensus-critical paths where latency is paramount, the hybrid approach preserves sub-millisecond performance while gaining durability benefits for all other domain events.\n\n**Recommendation:** Proceed with the migration plan, prioritizing Phase 1 (Outbox Foundation) to establish the consistency mechanism before introducing external broker dependencies.\n\n---\n\n## Appendix A: File References\n\n| Component | File Path |\n|-----------|-----------|\n| ADR-003 Event-Driven Communication | `docs/adr/003-event-driven-module-communication.md` |\n| Architecture Overview | `docs/architecture.md` |\n| IEventBus Interface (Core) | `src/UtilityChain.Core/Abstractions/IEventBus.cs` |\n| InMemoryEventBus Implementation | `src/UtilityChain.Core/Services/InMemoryEventBus.cs` |\n| StakingService | `src/UtilityChain.Staking/StakingService.cs` |\n| GovernanceService | `src/UtilityChain.Governance/GovernanceService.cs` |\n| TransactionProcessor | `src/UtilityChain.TransactionProcessing/TransactionProcessor.cs` |\n| P2PService | `src/UtilityChain.Networking/P2PService.cs` |\n| TokenService | `src/UtilityChain.Tokens/TokenService.cs` |\n| ConsensusContext | `src/UtilityChain.Consensus/ConsensusContext.cs` |\n| WorldState | `src/UtilityChain.Core/State/WorldState.cs` |\n| GatewayController | `src/UtilityChain.ApiGateway/GatewayController.cs` |\n| Node Startup | `src/UtilityChain.Node/Startup.cs` |\n| Node Program | `src/UtilityChain.Node/Program.cs` |\n| appsettings.json | `src/UtilityChain.Node/appsettings.json` |\n\n---\n\n*End of Technical Design Proposal*\n",

{
  "content": "# Technical Design Proposal: Migration from In-Memory Event Bus to External Message Broker\n\n**Document ID:** PROPOSAL-2026-001\n**Project:** UtilityChain Core Suite\n**Author:** Senior Solutions Architect\n**Date:** February 2, 2026\n**Status:** Draft for Review\n\n---\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nThis proposal outlines a comprehensive migration strategy for the UtilityChain Core Suite's inter-service communication infrastructure. The current `InMemoryEventBus` implementation, while performant for single-node deployments, presents significant scalability and resilience limitations as the platform approaches mainnet launch. This document details the technical approach, affected components, consistency patterns, configuration changes, error handling strategies, and architectural trade-offs for migrating to an external message broker.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Analysis of Current Architecture\n\n### 1.1 Current Implementation Overview\n\nAs documented in **ADR-003 (Event-Driven Module Communication)** at `docs/adr/003-event-driven-module-communication.md`, the UtilityChain Core Suite employs a lightweight, in-memory Domain Event Bus following the Mediator and Observer patterns. The system was intentionally designed for in-process communication to achieve:\n\n- **Zero-copy data-flow** for maximum throughput\n- **Sub-millisecond latency** for consensus-critical operations\n- **Single-binary deployment** without external dependencies\n\n### 1.2 IEventBus Interface Contracts\n\nThe codebase contains multiple `IEventBus` interface definitions, reflecting the modular monolith architecture:\n\n**Core Abstractions** (`src/UtilityChain.Core/Abstractions/IEventBus.cs:43-88`):\n```csharp\npublic interface IEventBus\n{\n    ValueTask PublishAsync<TEvent>(TEvent @event, CancellationToken ct = default)\n        where TEvent : class, IEvent;\n\n    SubscriptionToken Subscribe<TEvent>(\n        Func<TEvent, CancellationToken, ValueTask> handler,\n        SubscriptionOptions? options = null)\n        where TEvent : class, IEvent;\n\n    void Unsubscribe(in SubscriptionToken token);\n}\n```\n\n**Core Services Implementation** (`src/UtilityChain.Core/Services/InMemoryEventBus.cs:36-75`):\n```csharp\npublic interface IEventBus : IAsyncDisposable, IDisposable\n{\n    IDisposable Subscribe<TEvent>(\n        Func<TEvent, CancellationToken, ValueTask> handler,\n        string? subscriberId = null)\n        where TEvent : IEvent;\n\n    ValueTask PublishAsync<TEvent>(TEvent @event, CancellationToken cancellationToken = default)\n        where TEvent : IEvent;\n\n    bool HasSubscribers(Type eventType);\n}\n```\n\n### 1.3 InMemoryEventBus Implementation Characteristics\n\nThe primary implementation at `src/UtilityChain.Core/Services/InMemoryEventBus.cs:82-351` exhibits these characteristics:\n\n1. **Channel-Based Architecture**: Uses `System.Threading.Channels.Channel<EventEnvelope>` with bounded capacity (default 65,536)\n2. **Multi-Dispatcher Model**: Spawns `Environment.ProcessorCount` dispatcher tasks for parallel processing\n3. **Fire-and-Forget Delivery**: Each handler executes via `Task.Run()` independently (lines 262-281)\n4. **Weak Reference Subscriptions**: Prevents memory leaks but complicates handler lifecycle management\n5. **In-Process Only**: All communication occurs within the same address space\n\n**Critical Limitation:** The synchronous coupling between state mutations and event publication creates an atomic boundary that will be broken when introducing an external broker.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Affected Components (IEventBus Usage Analysis)\n\n### 2.1 Services That Publish Events\n\n| Service | File Location | Events Published | Nature of Changes Required |\n|---------|--------------|------------------|---------------------------|\n| **StakingService** | `src/UtilityChain.Staking/StakingService.cs:31,50,93,136,208` | `StakeCreatedEvent`, `StakeWithdrawnEvent`, `RewardsClaimedEvent` | Implement outbox pattern for stake operations |\n| **GovernanceService** | `src/UtilityChain.Governance/GovernanceService.cs:36,44,80,130,199` | `ProposalCreatedEvent`, `VoteCastEvent`, `ProposalFinalizedEvent` | Wrap proposal/vote transactions with outbox writes |\n| **TransactionProcessor** | `src/UtilityChain.TransactionProcessing/TransactionProcessor.cs:29,43,125,134,163` | `TransactionRejectedEvent`, `TransactionAcceptedEvent` | Critical path - requires careful outbox integration |\n| **P2PService** | `src/UtilityChain.Networking/P2PService.cs:34,44,240,268,348` | `PeerConnectedEvent`, `PeerDisconnectedEvent`, `NetworkMessageEvent` | Network events can tolerate eventual consistency |\n| **TokenService** | `src/UtilityChain.Tokens/TokenService.cs:27,39,63,98` | `TokenCreatedEvent`, `TokenMintedEvent`, `TokenBurnedEvent`, `TokenTransferredEvent` | Must coordinate with token state persistence |\n| **ConsensusContext** | `src/UtilityChain.Consensus/ConsensusContext.cs:41,58,235` | `BlockProposedEvent` | Consensus-critical; may require hybrid approach |\n| **WorldState** | `src/UtilityChain.Core/State/WorldState.cs:140,152,284` | `WorldStateCommittedEvent` | State root publication must be atomic with commit |\n| **GatewayController** | `src/UtilityChain.ApiGateway/GatewayController.cs:21,28,91,161,196` | `TransactionReceived`, `ContractDeployed`, `ContractInvoked` | API events can be published asynchronously |\n\n### 2.2 Services That Subscribe to Events\n\n| Service | Events Subscribed | Critical Path? |\n|---------|------------------|----------------|\n| **StakingService** | `NewBlockEvent` (line 65) | Yes - reward calculations |\n| **GovernanceService** | `ProposalCreatedEvent`, `ProposalFinalizedEvent` (lines 52-53) | Yes - policy enforcement |\n| **ConsensusContext** | `BlockCommittedEvent`, `VoteReceivedEvent` (lines 80-81) | Critical - consensus integrity |\n| **TokenService** | `BlockMinedEvent` (line 98) | Yes - balance commits |\n| **NodeRuntimeCoordinator** | `NodePanicEvent` (`Startup.cs:241`) | Critical - node lifecycle |\n\n### 2.3 Summary of Changes by Severity\n\n**High Impact (Requires Transactional Outbox):**\n- `TransactionProcessor` - Transaction acceptance must be atomic with event publication\n- `StakingService` - Stake operations affect account balances\n- `GovernanceService` - Votes must be recorded durably before notification\n- `WorldState` - State root changes are authoritative\n\n**Medium Impact (Requires Reliable Publishing):**\n- `TokenService` - Token operations should be durable\n- `ConsensusContext` - Block proposals need reliable delivery\n\n**Low Impact (Fire-and-Forget Acceptable):**\n- `P2PService` - Network events are observational\n- `GatewayController` - API notifications are advisory\n\n---\n\n## 3. Asynchronicity and Data Consistency: The Transactional Outbox Pattern\n\n### 3.1 The Atomicity Problem\n\nThe current `InMemoryEventBus` provides implicit atomicity: if `PublishAsync` succeeds, the event is delivered (assuming the process doesn't crash). Consider this flow in `TransactionProcessor.cs:141-163`:\n\n```csharp\n// Current Flow (PROBLEMATIC with external broker):\nawait _repository.AddPendingAsync(tx, ct);  // Step 1: Persist\nawait _eventBus.PublishAsync(new TransactionAcceptedEvent(tx), ct);  // Step 2: Publish\n```\n\nWith an external broker, this creates a dual-write problem:\n- If Step 1 succeeds but Step 2 fails (network partition), the transaction is persisted but never announced\n- If Step 2 succeeds but Step 1 fails (DB error), an event is published for a non-existent transaction\n\n### 3.2 Proposed Solution: Transactional Outbox Pattern\n\nThe **Transactional Outbox Pattern** ensures atomicity by writing events to a local \"outbox\" table within the same database transaction as the business operation. A separate background process (\"Outbox Publisher\") then reliably forwards these events to the external broker.\n\n#### 3.2.1 Outbox Entity Design\n\n```csharp\n// src/UtilityChain.Core/Outbox/OutboxMessage.cs\nnamespace UtilityChain.Core.Outbox;\n\npublic sealed class OutboxMessage\n{\n    public Guid Id { get; init; } = Guid.NewGuid();\n    public string EventType { get; init; } = default!;\n    public string Payload { get; init; } = default!;  // JSON-serialized event\n    public DateTimeOffset CreatedAt { get; init; } = DateTimeOffset.UtcNow;\n    public DateTimeOffset? ProcessedAt { get; set; }\n    public int RetryCount { get; set; }\n    public string? LastError { get; set; }\n    public OutboxMessageStatus Status { get; set; } = OutboxMessageStatus.Pending;\n}\n\npublic enum OutboxMessageStatus\n{\n    Pending,\n    Processing,\n    Completed,\n    Failed\n}\n```\n\n#### 3.2.2 Outbox Repository Interface\n\n```csharp\n// src/UtilityChain.Core/Outbox/IOutboxRepository.cs\nnamespace UtilityChain.Core.Outbox;\n\npublic interface IOutboxRepository\n{\n    Task AddAsync(OutboxMessage message, CancellationToken ct = default);\n    Task<IReadOnlyList<OutboxMessage>> GetPendingAsync(int batchSize, CancellationToken ct = default);\n    Task MarkAsProcessedAsync(Guid id, CancellationToken ct = default);\n    Task MarkAsFailedAsync(Guid id, string error, CancellationToken ct = default);\n}\n```\n\n#### 3.2.3 Modified Transaction Processing Flow\n\n```csharp\n// src/UtilityChain.TransactionProcessing/TransactionProcessor.cs (Modified)\nprivate async Task HandleTransactionAsync(TransactionEnvelope envelope, CancellationToken ct)\n{\n    var tx = envelope.Transaction;\n\n    // ... validation logic ...\n\n    // CRITICAL CHANGE: Use database transaction for atomicity\n    await using var dbTransaction = await _repository.BeginTransactionAsync(ct);\n    try\n    {\n        // Step 1: Persist transaction\n        await _repository.AddPendingAsync(tx, ct);\n\n        // Step 2: Write to outbox (SAME transaction)\n        var outboxMessage = new OutboxMessage\n        {\n            EventType = typeof(TransactionAcceptedEvent).FullName!,\n            Payload = JsonSerializer.Serialize(new TransactionAcceptedEvent(tx))\n        };\n        await _outboxRepository.AddAsync(outboxMessage, ct);\n\n        // Step 3: Commit both together\n        await dbTransaction.CommitAsync(ct);\n    }\n    catch\n    {\n        await dbTransaction.RollbackAsync(ct);\n        throw;\n    }\n\n    // Event will be published by OutboxPublisher background service\n}\n```\n\n#### 3.2.4 Outbox Publisher Background Service\n\n```csharp\n// src/UtilityChain.Infrastructure/Messaging/OutboxPublisher.cs\nnamespace UtilityChain.Infrastructure.Messaging;\n\npublic sealed class OutboxPublisher : BackgroundService\n{\n    private readonly IOutboxRepository _outboxRepository;\n    private readonly IMessageBrokerClient _brokerClient;\n    private readonly ILogger<OutboxPublisher> _logger;\n    private readonly OutboxPublisherOptions _options;\n\n    protected override async Task ExecuteAsync(CancellationToken stoppingToken)\n    {\n        while (!stoppingToken.IsCancellationRequested)\n        {\n            try\n            {\n                var messages = await _outboxRepository\n                    .GetPendingAsync(_options.BatchSize, stoppingToken);\n\n                foreach (var message in messages)\n                {\n                    try\n                    {\n                        await _brokerClient.PublishAsync(\n                            message.EventType,\n                            message.Payload,\n                            stoppingToken);\n\n                        await _outboxRepository.MarkAsProcessedAsync(message.Id, stoppingToken);\n                    }\n                    catch (Exception ex)\n                    {\n                        _logger.LogError(ex,\n                            \"Failed to publish outbox message {MessageId}\", message.Id);\n                        await _outboxRepository.MarkAsFailedAsync(\n                            message.Id, ex.Message, stoppingToken);\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n            catch (Exception ex)\n            {\n                _logger.LogError(ex, \"Outbox publisher iteration failed\");\n            }\n\n            await Task.Delay(_options.PollingInterval, stoppingToken);\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### 3.3 Consistency Guarantees\n\n| Scenario | Behavior with Outbox Pattern |\n|----------|------------------------------|\n| DB commit succeeds, broker unavailable | Event stored in outbox, delivered when broker recovers |\n| DB commit fails | No outbox entry, no event published (consistent) |\n| Outbox publisher crashes mid-batch | Uncommitted messages remain pending, re-processed on restart |\n| Duplicate delivery to broker | Consumers must be idempotent (handled via event ID) |\n\n---\n\n## 4. Configuration and Dependency Management\n\n### 4.1 appsettings.json Modifications\n\nCurrent configuration at `src/UtilityChain.Node/appsettings.json:97-103`:\n```json\n\"EventBus\": {\n  \"MaxDelayMilliseconds\": 30000,\n          \"ExponentialBackoff\": true\n        }\n      },\n      \"MessageBroker\": {\n        \"Provider\": \"RabbitMQ\",\n        \"RabbitMQ\": {\n \"CleanupIntervalHours\": 24,\n        \"RetentionDays\": 7\n      }\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### 4.2 Startup.cs / Program.cs Modifications\n\n**Current Registration** (`src/UtilityChain.Node/Startup.cs:101`):\n```csharp\nservices.AddSingleton<IEventBus, InMemoryEventBus>();\n```\n\n**Proposed Registration:**\n```csharp\n// src/UtilityChain.Node/Startup.cs (Modified)\nusing Microsoft.Extensions.DependencyInjection;\nusing UtilityChain.Infrastructure.Messaging;\nusing UtilityChain.Infrastructure.Messaging.RabbitMQ;\nusing UtilityChain.Core.Outbox;\n\npublic static class EventBusServiceExtensions\n{\n    public static IServiceCollection AddEventBusInfrastructure(\n        this IServiceCollection services,\n        IConfiguration configuration)\n    {\n        // Bind options\n        services.Configure<MessageBrokerOptions>(\n            configuration.GetSection(\"UtilityChain:Node:MessageBroker\"));\n        services.Configure<OutboxOptions>(\n            configuration.GetSection(\"UtilityChain:Node:Outbox\"));\n\n        // Register outbox infrastructure\n        services.AddScoped<IOutboxRepository, SqliteOutboxRepository>();\n        services.AddHostedService<OutboxPublisher>();\n        services.AddHostedService<OutboxCleanupService>();\n\n        // Register message broker client\n        var brokerProvider = configuration\n            .GetValue<string>(\"UtilityChain:Node:MessageBroker:Provider\");\n\n        switch (brokerProvider?.ToLowerInvariant())\n        {\n            case \"rabbitmq\":\n                services.AddSingleton<IMessageBrokerClient, RabbitMQClient>();\n                services.AddSingleton<IEventBus, RabbitMQEventBus>();\n .AddKafka(name: \"kafka\", tags: new[] { \"messaging\" });\n                break;\n\n            case \"inmemory\":\n            default:\n                // Fallback for development/testing\n                services.AddSingleton<IEventBus, InMemoryEventBus>();\n                break;\n        }\n\n        // Register dead-letter queue handler\n        services.AddHostedService<DeadLetterQueueProcessor>();\n\n        return services;\n    }\n}\n\n// In BuildHost method:\n.ConfigureServices((ctx, services) =>\n{\n    // ... existing registrations ...\n})\n```\n\n### 4.3 RabbitMQ Client Implementation Skeleton\n\n```csharp\n// src/UtilityChain.Infrastructure/Messaging/RabbitMQ/RabbitMQEventBus.cs\nnamespace UtilityChain.Infrastructure.Messaging.RabbitMQ;\n\npublic sealed class RabbitMQEventBus : IEventBus, IAsyncDisposable\n{\n    private readonly IConnection _connection;\n    private readonly IModel _publishChannel;\n    private readonly ConcurrentDictionary<Type, IModel> _consumeChannels;\n    private readonly MessageBrokerOptions _options;\n    private readonly ILogger<RabbitMQEventBus> _logger;\n    private readonly JsonSerializerOptions _jsonOptions;\n\n    public RabbitMQEventBus(\n        IOptions<MessageBrokerOptions> options,\n        ILogger<RabbitMQEventBus> logger)\n    {\n        _options = options.Value;\n        _logger = logger;\n        _jsonOptions = new JsonSerializerOptions\n        {\n            PropertyNamingPolicy = JsonNamingPolicy.CamelCase\n        };\n        _consumeChannels = new();\n\n        var factory = new ConnectionFactory\n        {\n            HostName = _options.RabbitMQ.HostName,\n            Port = _options.RabbitMQ.Port,\n            VirtualHost = _options.RabbitMQ.VirtualHost,\n            UserName = _options.RabbitMQ.UserName,\n            Password = _options.RabbitMQ.Password,\n            AutomaticRecoveryEnabled = true,\n            NetworkRecoveryInterval = TimeSpan.FromSeconds(10)\n        };\n\n        _connection = factory.CreateConnection();\n        _publishChannel = _connection.CreateModel();\n\n        // Enable publisher confirms for reliable delivery\n        _publishChannel.ConfirmSelect();\n\n        DeclareTopology();\n    }\n\n    public async ValueTask PublishAsync<TEvent>(\n        TEvent @event,\n        CancellationToken cancellationToken = default)\n        where TEvent : IEvent\n    {\n        var routingKey = GetRoutingKey(typeof(TEvent));\n        var body = JsonSerializer.SerializeToUtf8Bytes(@event, _jsonOptions);\n\n        var properties = _publishChannel.CreateBasicProperties();\n        properties.DeliveryMode = 2; // Persistent\n        properties.MessageId = Guid.NewGuid().ToString();\n        properties.Timestamp = new AmqpTimestamp(DateTimeOffset.UtcNow.ToUnixTimeSeconds());\n        properties.Type = typeof(TEvent).FullName;\n\n        _publishChannel.BasicPublish(\n            exchange: _options.Exchanges.DomainEvents.Name,\n            routingKey: routingKey,\n            basicProperties: properties,\n            body: body);\n\n        // Wait for broker acknowledgment\n        _publishChannel.WaitForConfirmsOrDie(TimeSpan.FromSeconds(5));\n\n        await Task.CompletedTask;\n    }\n\n    public IDisposable Subscribe<TEvent>(\n        Func<TEvent, CancellationToken, ValueTask> handler,\n        string? subscriberId = null)\n        where TEvent : IEvent\n    {\n        var eventType = typeof(TEvent);\n        var queueName = GetQueueName(eventType);\n\n        var channel = _connection.CreateModel();\n        _consumeChannels[eventType] = channel;\n\n        var consumer = new AsyncEventingBasicConsumer(channel);\n        consumer.Received += async (model, ea) =>\n        {\n            try\n            {\n                var @event = JsonSerializer.Deserialize<TEvent>(ea.Body.Span, _jsonOptions);\n                if (@event != null)\n                {\n                    await handler(@event, CancellationToken.None);\n                }\n                channel.BasicAck(ea.DeliveryTag, false);\n            }\n            catch (Exception ex)\n            {\n                _logger.LogError(ex, \"Error processing message {MessageId}\", ea.BasicProperties.MessageId);\n                // Negative acknowledgment - message will go to DLQ\n                channel.BasicNack(ea.DeliveryTag, false, false);\n            }\n        };\n\n        channel.BasicConsume(queue: queueName, autoAck: false, consumer: consumer);\n\n        return new SubscriptionHandle(() =>\n        {\n            if (_consumeChannels.TryRemove(eventType, out var ch))\n            {\n                ch.Close();\n                ch.Dispose();\n            }\n        });\n    }\n\n    private void DeclareTopology()\n    {\n        // Declare main exchange\n        _publishChannel.ExchangeDeclare(\n            exchange: _options.Exchanges.DomainEvents.Name,\n            type: _options.Exchanges.DomainEvents.Type,\n            durable: true);\n\n        // Declare dead-letter exchange\n        _publishChannel.ExchangeDeclare(\n            exchange: _options.Exchanges.DeadLetter.Name,\n            type: \"fanout\",\n            durable: true);\n\n        // Declare dead-letter queue\n        _publishChannel.QueueDeclare(\n            queue: \"utilitychain.dlq\",\n            durable: true,\n            exclusive: false,\n            autoDelete: false);\n        _publishChannel.QueueBind(\"utilitychain.dlq\", _options.Exchanges.DeadLetter.Name, \"\");\n\n        // Declare application queues with DLX binding\n        foreach (var queueConfig in _options.Queues.Values)\n        {\n            var args = new Dictionary<string, object>\n            {\n                [\"x-dead-letter-exchange\"] = _options.Exchanges.DeadLetter.Name\n            };\n\n            if (queueConfig.MessageTtlSeconds > 0)\n            {\n                args[\"x-message-ttl\"] = queueConfig.MessageTtlSeconds * 1000;\n            }\n\n            _publishChannel.QueueDeclare(\n                queue: queueConfig.Name,\n                durable: queueConfig.Durable,\n                exclusive: false,\n                autoDelete: false,\n                arguments: args);\n\n            foreach (var routingKey in queueConfig.RoutingKeys)\n            {\n                _publishChannel.QueueBind(\n                    queueConfig.Name,\n                    _options.Exchanges.DomainEvents.Name,\n                    routingKey);\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    private static string GetRoutingKey(Type eventType)\n    {\n        // Example: TransactionAcceptedEvent -> transaction.accepted\n        var name = eventType.Name.Replace(\"Event\", \"\");\n        return string.Join(\".\",\n            System.Text.RegularExpressions.Regex\n                .Split(name, \"(?<!^)(?=[A-Z])\")\n                .Select(s => s.ToLowerInvariant()));\n    }\n\n    public async ValueTask DisposeAsync()\n    {\n        foreach (var channel in _consumeChannels.Values)\n        {\n            channel.Close();\n            channel.Dispose();\n        }\n        _publishChannel.Close();\n        _publishChannel.Dispose();\n        _connection.Close();\n        _connection.Dispose();\n        await Task.CompletedTask;\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. Resilience and Error Handling\n\n### 5.1 New Failure Modes with External Broker\n\n| Failure Mode | Description | Impact | Mitigation |\n|--------------|-------------|--------|------------|\n| **Network Partition** | Node loses connectivity to broker | Events queued in outbox, not delivered | Outbox pattern with local persistence |\n| **Broker Downtime** | RabbitMQ/Kafka cluster unavailable | All event publishing blocked | Connection retry with exponential backoff |\n| **Message Expiration** | TTL exceeded before consumption | Events lost | Dead-letter queue for inspection |\n| **Poison Messages** | Malformed events causing consumer failures | Consumer stuck in retry loop | Dead-letter after N retries |\n| **Consumer Lag** | Consumers slower than publishers | Queue growth, memory pressure | Prefetch limits, consumer scaling |\n| **Duplicate Delivery** | Broker redelivers after timeout | Handler invoked multiple times | Idempotent handlers (deduplication) |\n\n### 5.2 Dead-Letter Queue (DLQ) Strategy\n\nMessages that cannot be processed after exhausting retry attempts are routed to a Dead-Letter Queue for manual inspection and replay.\n\n```csharp\n// src/UtilityChain.Infrastructure/Messaging/DeadLetterQueueProcessor.cs\nnamespace UtilityChain.Infrastructure.Messaging;\n\npublic sealed class DeadLetterQueueProcessor : BackgroundService\n{\n    private readonly IMessageBrokerClient _brokerClient;\n    private readonly IDeadLetterRepository _dlqRepository;\n    private readonly ILogger<DeadLetterQueueProcessor> _logger;\n\n    protected override async Task ExecuteAsync(CancellationToken stoppingToken)\n    {\n        await _brokerClient.ConsumeAsync<DeadLetterMessage>(\n            \"utilitychain.dlq\",\n            async (message, ct) =>\n            {\n                _logger.LogWarning(\n                    \"Dead letter received: Type={EventType}, OriginalError={Error}\",\n                    message.OriginalType,\n                    message.LastError);\n\n                // Persist for manual review/replay\n                await _dlqRepository.StoreAsync(new DeadLetterRecord\n                {\n                    Id = Guid.NewGuid(),\n                    OriginalEventType = message.OriginalType,\n                    Payload = message.Payload,\n                    FailedAt = DateTimeOffset.UtcNow,\n                    RetryCount = message.RetryCount,\n                    LastError = message.LastError,\n                    OriginalQueue = message.OriginalQueue\n                }, ct);\n            },\n            stoppingToken);\n    }\n}\n\npublic interface IDeadLetterRepository\n{\n    Task StoreAsync(DeadLetterRecord record, CancellationToken ct);\n    Task<IReadOnlyList<DeadLetterRecord>> GetPendingReplayAsync(int limit, CancellationToken ct);\n    Task ReplayAsync(Guid id, CancellationToken ct);\n    Task DiscardAsync(Guid id, string reason, CancellationToken ct);\n}\n```\n\n### 5.3 Retry Policies with Polly\n\n```csharp\n// src/UtilityChain.Infrastructure/Messaging/ResiliencePolicies.cs\nusing Polly;\nusing Polly.Retry;\n\nnamespace UtilityChain.Infrastructure.Messaging;\n\npublic static class ResiliencePolicies\n{\n    public static AsyncRetryPolicy CreatePublishPolicy(ILogger logger, RetryPolicyOptions options)\n    {\n        return Policy\n            .Handle<BrokerUnreachableException>()\n            .Or<AlreadyClosedException>()\n            .Or<IOException>()\n            .WaitAndRetryAsync(\n                retryCount: options.RetryCount,\n                sleepDurationProvider: attempt =>\n                {\n                    var delay = TimeSpan.FromMilliseconds(\n                        Math.Min(\n                            options.BaseDelayMilliseconds * Math.Pow(2, attempt),\n                            options.MaxDelayMilliseconds));\n\n                    // Add jitter to prevent thundering herd\n                    var jitter = TimeSpan.FromMilliseconds(\n                        Random.Shared.Next(0, (int)(delay.TotalMilliseconds * 0.1)));\n\n                    return delay + jitter;\n                },\n                onRetry: (exception, delay, attempt, context) =>\n                {\n                    logger.LogWarning(exception,\n                        \"Event publish attempt {Attempt} failed. Retrying in {Delay}ms\",\n                        attempt, delay.TotalMilliseconds);\n                });\n    }\n\n    public static AsyncRetryPolicy CreateConsumePolicy(ILogger logger, int maxRetries)\n    {\n        return Policy\n            .Handle<Exception>(ex => !(ex is OperationCanceledException))\n            .WaitAndRetryAsync(\n                retryCount: maxRetries,\n                sleepDurationProvider: attempt =>\n                    TimeSpan.FromSeconds(Math.Pow(2, attempt)),\n                onRetry: (exception, delay, attempt, context) =>\n                {\n                    logger.LogWarning(exception,\n                        \"Event consumption attempt {Attempt} failed. Retrying in {Delay}s\",\n                        attempt, delay.TotalSeconds);\n                });\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### 5.4 Idempotent Event Handlers\n\nTo handle duplicate deliveries, consumers must be idempotent:\n\n```csharp\n// Example: Idempotent StakingService event handler\npublic class IdempotentStakingEventHandler : IEventHandler<StakeCreatedEvent>\n{\n    private readonly IProcessedEventRepository _processedEvents;\n    private readonly IStakeAggregator _aggregator;\n\n    public async ValueTask HandleAsync(StakeCreatedEvent @event, CancellationToken ct)\n    {\n        // Check if already processed\n        var eventId = @event.EventId; // Events should carry a unique ID\n        if (await _processedEvents.ExistsAsync(eventId, ct))\n        {\n            return; // Idempotent: skip duplicate\n        }\n\n        // Process the event\n        await _aggregator.ApplyStakeAsync(@event.Stake, ct);\n\n        // Mark as processed\n        await _processedEvents.MarkAsync(eventId, ct);\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 6. Architectural Trade-offs\n\n### 6.1 Advantages of External Message Broker\n\n| Benefit | Description |\n|---------|-------------|\n| **Horizontal Scalability** | Multiple node instances can publish/consume independently, enabling cluster deployments |\n| **Temporal Decoupling** | Publishers and consumers operate independently; consumers can catch up after downtime |\n| **Durable Message Storage** | Messages persist in broker until acknowledged, surviving node restarts |\n| **Independent Deployments** | Services can be updated without coordinating all components simultaneously |\n| **Observability** | Broker management consoles provide queue depths, throughput metrics, consumer lag visibility |\n| **Replay Capability** | Ability to replay events from DLQ or persistent topics (Kafka) for debugging or reprocessing |\n| **Multi-Protocol Support** | External clients (monitoring, analytics) can subscribe without coupling to .NET internals |\n\n### 6.2 Disadvantages and New Complexities\n\n| Drawback | Description | Mitigation |\n|----------|-------------|------------|\n| **Increased Latency** | Network round-trips add 1-10ms overhead vs. in-memory microseconds | Accept for non-critical paths; hybrid approach for consensus |\n| **Operational Complexity** | New infrastructure to deploy, monitor, and maintain | Infrastructure-as-Code, managed services (CloudAMQP, Confluent Cloud) |\n| **Data Consistency Complexity** | Dual-write problem requires outbox pattern | Implement as described in Section 3 |\n| **Eventual Consistency** | Consumers may see events with delay | Design handlers for idempotency; use compensation patterns |\n| **New Failure Modes** | Broker failures, network partitions, poison messages | DLQ, retries, circuit breakers (Section 5) |\n| **Cost** | Additional infrastructure cost (VMs, managed services) | Size appropriately; start with single-node broker for consortium |\n| **Message Ordering** | Global ordering not guaranteed across partitions/queues | Use partition keys for ordered streams where required |\n| **Serialization Overhead** | Events must be serialized to JSON/Protobuf | Use efficient serializers; schema registry for versioning |\n\n### 6.3 Hybrid Approach Recommendation\n\nFor **consensus-critical events** (block proposals, vote collection), consider maintaining a supplementary in-process channel:\n\n```csharp\npublic sealed class HybridEventBus : IEventBus\n{\n    private readonly InMemoryEventBus _inProcess;\n    private readonly RabbitMQEventBus _distributed;\n    private readonly HashSet<Type> _localOnlyTypes = new()\n    {\n        typeof(VoteReceivedEvent),\n        typeof(BlockProposedEvent)\n    };\n\n    public async ValueTask PublishAsync<TEvent>(TEvent @event, CancellationToken ct)\n        where TEvent : IEvent\n    {\n        // Consensus-critical events: local only for latency\n        if (_localOnlyTypes.Contains(typeof(TEvent)))\n        {\n            await _inProcess.PublishAsync(@event, ct);\n            return;\n        }\n\n        // All other events: distributed for durability\n        await _distributed.PublishAsync(@event, ct);\n\n        // Optionally also publish locally for immediate in-node handling\n        await _inProcess.PublishAsync(@event, ct);\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 7. Migration Plan Summary\n\n### Phase 1: Foundation (Week 1-2)\n1. Implement `IOutboxRepository` with SQLite/PostgreSQL backing\n2. Create `OutboxMessage` entity and database migrations\n3. Build `OutboxPublisher` background service\n4. Add comprehensive unit tests for outbox patterns\n\n### Phase 2: Broker Integration (Week 3-4)\n1. Implement `IMessageBrokerClient` interface\n2. Build `RabbitMQEventBus` implementation\n3. Configure queue topology (exchanges, queues, DLX)\n4. Set up local RabbitMQ for development\n\n### Phase 3: Service Migration (Week 5-7)\n1. Migrate low-risk services first (P2PService, GatewayController)\n2. Add outbox writes to medium-risk services (TokenService, GovernanceService)\n3. Migrate high-risk services (TransactionProcessor, StakingService)\n4. Implement hybrid approach for ConsensusContext\n\n### Phase 4: Testing & Hardening (Week 8)\n1. Chaos testing (broker failures, network partitions)\n2. Load testing with production-like traffic\n3. DLQ monitoring and alerting\n4. Runbook documentation for operations\n\n### Phase 5: Production Rollout (Week 9-10)\n1. Deploy broker infrastructure\n2. Feature flag rollout (gradual traffic shift)\n3. Monitor queue depths and consumer lag\n4. Full cutover and InMemoryEventBus deprecation\n\n---\n\n## 8. Conclusion\n\nThe migration from `InMemoryEventBus` to an external message broker represents a significant architectural evolution for the UtilityChain Core Suite. While introducing operational complexity and new failure modes, the benefits of scalability, resilience, and independent deployability are essential for mainnet readiness.\n\nThe **Transactional Outbox Pattern** is the cornerstone of this migration, ensuring data consistency despite the inherently asynchronous nature of distributed messaging. Combined with robust retry policies, dead-letter queues, and idempotent consumers, the proposed architecture provides enterprise-grade reliability.\n\nFor consensus-critical paths where latency is paramount, the hybrid approach preserves sub-millisecond performance while gaining durability benefits for all other domain events.\n\n**Recommendation:** Proceed with the migration plan, prioritizing Phase 1 (Outbox Foundation) to establish the consistency mechanism before introducing external broker dependencies.\n\n---\n\n## Appendix A: File References\n\n| Component | File Path |\n|-----------|-----------|\n| ADR-003 Event-Driven Communication | `docs/adr/003-event-driven-module-communication.md` |\n| Architecture Overview | `docs/architecture.md` |\n| IEventBus Interface (Core) | `src/UtilityChain.Core/Abstractions/IEventBus.cs` |\n| InMemoryEventBus Implementation | `src/UtilityChain.Core/Services/InMemoryEventBus.cs` |\n| StakingService | `src/UtilityChain.Staking/StakingService.cs` |\n| GovernanceService | `src/UtilityChain.Governance/GovernanceService.cs` |\n| TransactionProcessor | `src/UtilityChain.TransactionProcessing/TransactionProcessor.cs` |\n| P2PService | `src/UtilityChain.Networking/P2PService.cs` |\n| TokenService | `src/UtilityChain.Tokens/TokenService.cs` |\n| ConsensusContext | `src/UtilityChain.Consensus/ConsensusContext.cs` |\n| WorldState | `src/UtilityChain.Core/State/WorldState.cs` |\n| GatewayController | `src/UtilityChain.ApiGateway/GatewayController.cs` |\n| Node Startup | `src/UtilityChain.Node/Startup.cs` |\n| Node Program | `src/UtilityChain.Node/Program.cs` |\n| appsettings.json | `src/UtilityChain.Node/appsettings.json` |\n\n---\n\n*End of Technical Design Proposal*\n",

# Technical Design Proposal: Migration from In-Memory Event Bus to External Message Broker

**Document ID:** PROPOSAL-2026-001
**Project:** UtilityChain Core Suite
**Author:** Senior Solutions Architect
**Date:** February 2, 2026
**Status:** Draft for Review

---

## Executive Summary

This proposal outlines a comprehensive migration strategy for the UtilityChain Core Suite's inter-service communication infrastructure. The current `InMemoryEventBus` implementation, while performant for single-node deployments, presents significant scalability and resilience limitations as the platform approaches mainnet launch. This document details the technical approach, affected components, consistency patterns, configuration changes, error handling strategies, and architectural trade-offs for migrating to an external message broker.

---

## 1. Analysis of Current Architecture

### 1.1 Current Implementation Overview

As documented in **ADR-003 (Event-Driven Module Communication)** at `docs/adr/003-event-driven-module-communication.md`, the UtilityChain Core Suite employs a lightweight, in-memory Domain Event Bus following the Mediator and Observer patterns. The system was intentionally designed for in-process communication to achieve:

- **Zero-copy data-flow** for maximum throughput
- **Sub-millisecond latency** for consensus-critical operations
- **Single-binary deployment** without external dependencies

### 1.2 IEventBus Interface Contracts

The codebase contains multiple `IEventBus` interface definitions, reflecting the modular monolith architecture:

**Core Abstractions** (`src/UtilityChain.Core/Abstractions/IEventBus.cs:43-88`):
```csharp
public interface IEventBus
{
    ValueTask PublishAsync<TEvent>(TEvent @event, CancellationToken ct = default)
        where TEvent : clas
... (truncated)
